This is a simple/basic k8s cluster architecture with 1 master node and multiple worker node. However, it is important for Kubernetes Cluster to be fault tolerance, therefore we can have multiple Master Node inside the same cluster as well.  ^8l2puEsV

Upgrade Version ^WO1joJvQ

We access this via kubectl, which allow us to
perform actions on pods, service, etc... ^0RGBCCQS

Work as configuration, where we can define:
1. number of CPU core. 
2. Memory
3. Other configurations ^vLKMpK9W

Check for the overall health of the whole cluster. 
Ensure workers are up and running the correct numbers of 
pods are running.  ^WLDgf2ke

Central distributed database, Key-Value store such as:
Current State, Desired State, Config of resources, etc...
It is a single source of truth of the database.  ^6PiuC8DV

Pod is the smallest unit of a K8s Cluster that wraps the container. We can have multiple containers inside 1 pod so that they can help each others to complete the job.  ^r3kHHluH

The container runtime run inside each node and
is responsible for running containers.  ^3PGZaAuC

Kube-proxy is a network proxy that runs on each node in the cluster. It is responsible for managing network connectivity, maintaining network rules across all nodes, pods, and containers inside the cluster, and also exposing services to the outside world. Kube-proxy is the core network component for entire Kubernetes cluster. ^ywqsee33

Think of the Service as the contract (“anyone hitting 10.0.0.123:443 should reach my-web-app”) and kube-proxy as the contractor actually wiring the cables so that packets follow the promise. Understanding the split clarifies debugging (Is my Service defined correctly? Is kube-proxy updating rules?) and guides design choices such as adopting eBPF-based networking for higher performance. ^n5Fv759e
